On Thu, 2008-02-21 at 12:20 -0800, Michael Rasmussen wrote:
> Wil Cooley wrote:
> > My habits for servers is to have to partitions: one for /boot and one
> > LVM Physical Volume. When I have two drives, these are (MD) RAID1
> > volumes; when I have two large drives, I create several partitions as
> > RAID1 volumes and use them as PVs in LVM. This allows me to not use them
> > until necessary and keep them stopped, so they don't try to sync if I
> > have to reboot uncleanly.
> 
> What is large?  How big do you make the physical volumes?
> 
> Think Mies van der Rohe.

I've done it with the 300GB drives in my main server. Rather than look
up how many DOS/BIOS logical partitions I could have in an extended
partition, I just used 4 primary partitions: 100M for the /boot mirror
and 3 PV mirrors divided kinda evenly from the remaining space.

Wil



From rsteff at comcast.net  Wed Feb 27 09:15:49 2008
From: rsteff at comcast.net (Richard C. Steffens)
Date: Wed, 27 Feb 2008 09:15:49 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Debugging odd effect a Slackware machine has on a network
	printer
Message-ID: <47C59AC5.6010101@comcast.net>

A number of years ago I started the project of sending audio from a the
sound card in a basement computer to the stereo in the living room. That
machine, which  was a 200 MHz Pentium running RH 7.0, finally  failed.
About a year ago I re-purposed another machine to replace it. I
installed Slackware on it (I forget which version) and things were back
to normal. Also, at the same time, my network printer started acting
funny. It would wake up, warm up, and then go back to sleep. I spent a
long time on the phone with Brother tech support, but never got a
satisfactory answer from them. I don't know what caused me to shut down
the basement machine, but when I did, the problem with the printer went
away, and has not returned.

Now that I have a little time, I'm ready to try to debug that problem. I
can set up the machine in my office so I won't have to run back and
forth to the basement.

I have very little time invested in running Slackware, and I realize
that I don't need X running on this machine, so I'm willing to start
from scratch. All the machine needs to do is to run Apache, MySQL, &
PHP, and be a file server.

Recommendations welcome as to the road to pursue: find and fix the
Slackware problem, or start over with a different distro.

-- 
Regards,

Dick Steffens



From creswick at gmail.com  Wed Feb 27 10:52:24 2008
From: creswick at gmail.com (Rogan Creswick)
Date: Wed, 27 Feb 2008 10:52:24 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Debugging odd effect a Slackware machine has on a
	network printer
In-Reply-To: <47C59AC5.6010101@comcast.net>
References: <47C59AC5.6010101@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <c834ec80802271052n5282c157xbb92334d7eeeed28@mail.gmail.com>

On Wed, Feb 27, 2008 at 9:15 AM, Richard C. Steffens <rsteff at comcast.net> wrote:
>
>  Recommendations welcome as to the road to pursue: find and fix the
>  Slackware problem, or start over with a different distro.
>

It has been my impression that slackware users are becoming rarer and
rarer these days, and either debian or RH based distros have the
strongest support 'net, so I would suggest using one of those.

Personally, I would strongly suggest Debian because of it's history of
stability, ease of maintenance, and tiered release cycles (stable /
testing / unstable).  Ubuntu has recently demonstrated that they care
more about meeting self-imposed deadlines than distributing usable
software, and Debian Lenny did a fine job when I recently installed it
on a T42p (wireless took 5-10 min of tweaking, but it got power
management and everything else I use working just fine).  The point
being that debian isn't as arduous as it used to be.

I can't speak for the RH derivatives, I've not used an rpm-based
distro since early '99.

I think you'll find it's a lot easier to get things working / fixed
with RH/deb. simply because more of us know how to use them.

--Rogan

>
> Now that I have a little time, I'm ready to try to debug that problem. I
> can set up the machine in my office so I won't have to run back and
> forth to the basement.
>
> I have very little time invested in running Slackware, and I realize
> that I don't need X running on this machine, so I'm willing to start
> from scratch. All the machine needs to do is to run Apache, MySQL, &
> PHP, and be a file server.
>
> Recommendations welcome as to the road to pursue: find and fix the
> Slackware problem, or start over with a different distro.
>
> --
> Regards,
>
> Dick Steffens
>

Did the Slackware server provide any services on your network? DHCP, CUPS,
or any or service?
If so, any of those could potentialy be causing the printer awaken (for a
new IP, or CUPS trying to access the printer, or something).
I would start by turning off un-needed services on the Slackware machine.
If all you need is SSH, Apache, and MySQL, then you can probably safely
disable any DHCP services, Portmap, CUPS, and any other services.

I'm an old Slackware user myself, don't have any boxes currently running it
but I do remember some tricks. I had never encountered a problem such as
this one.


-- 
Brent Jones
brent at servuhome.net

From lnxknight at gmail.com  Wed Feb 27 14:59:02 2008
From: lnxknight at gmail.com (Matt McKenzie)
Date: Wed, 27 Feb 2008 14:59:02 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Intel GMA X3100 vs. nVidia GeForce GS 256 MB
In-Reply-To: <47C5DD13.203@acm.org>
References: <47C5DD13.203@acm.org>
Message-ID: <da2207740802271459x631ec8cp87546de5d3dc4f81@mail.gmail.com>

On Wed, Feb 27, 2008 at 1:58 PM, Roderick A. Anderson <raanders at acm.org>
wrote:

> Quick insight.  Are there any reasons to prefer an Intel GMA X3100 over
>  a nVidia GeForce GS 256 MB, on a laptop running Ubuntu?
>
>
> Thanks,
> Rod
> --
>

It would help if you can give the model # of the NVidia card (and possibly
the laptop models).  GS is a sub-model, such as GS, GT, etc.  We need the
model #, such as 6150, 7600, 8800, etc. to better be able to compare.

Generally speaking though, NVidia or ATI discreet video with dedicated RAM
would tend to have better video performance than Intel with shared RAM.
I don't know if the GMA X3100 is different from other Intel video chips I
have no experience with that particular one.

In a laptop there can be power ramifications with using a dedicated video
vs. shared video.  There are things both ATI and NVidia do to mitigate that,
I know NVidia uses a thing called "Powermizer" to scale performance to
conserve battery life.  There is always a trade-off, better performance ==
less battery time, slower performance == better battery time.  Both ATI and
NVidia also have control panel settings you can adjust, but there aren't as
many options in the Linux version as in the Winders version usually.  I am
not sure about Intel if it has similar controls, it very well probably does,
I haven't seen it myself.


-- 
----------
Matt M.
LinuxKnight

Subject: [PLUG] alien ping response

We've been tracking down an intermittent, odd problem. One of the symptoms is
ping response behavior:


hostname % ping -I 1 -n 10.11.22.122 
 ...
64 bytes from 10.11.22.122: icmp_seq=1436. time=1. ms
64 bytes from 10.11.22.122: icmp_seq=1437. time=0. ms
64 bytes from 10.11.44.212: icmp_seq=1283. time=445990198. ms
64 bytes from 10.11.22.122: icmp_seq=1438. time=1. ms
64 bytes from 10.11.22.122: icmp_seq=1439. time=1. ms

What?  Why is the response from another device on another subnet arriving
here?

Have you seen behavior like this?
What was the cause?

From tim-pdxlug at sentinelchicken.org  Thu Feb 28 15:34:30 2008
From: tim-pdxlug at sentinelchicken.org (Tim)
Date: Thu, 28 Feb 2008 15:34:30 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] alien ping response
In-Reply-To: <20080228221731.GB9733@jamhome.us>
References: <20080228221731.GB9733@jamhome.us>
Message-ID: <20080228233430.GB2415@sentinelchicken.org>

Hi Michael,

On Thu, Feb 28, 2008 at 02:17:31PM -0800, Michael Rasmussen wrote:
> We've been tracking down an intermittent, odd problem. One of the symptoms is
> ping response behavior:
> 
> 
> hostname % ping -I 1 -n 10.11.22.122 
>  ...
> 64 bytes from 10.11.22.122: icmp_seq=1436. time=1. ms
> 64 bytes from 10.11.22.122: icmp_seq=1437. time=0. ms
> 64 bytes from 10.11.44.212: icmp_seq=1283. time=445990198. ms
> 64 bytes from 10.11.22.122: icmp_seq=1438. time=1. ms
> 64 bytes from 10.11.22.122: icmp_seq=1439. time=1. ms
> 
> What?  Why is the response from another device on another subnet arriving
> here?
> 
> Have you seen behavior like this?
> What was the cause?

Once upon a time in a college network I was working in, I saw this kind
of traffic: echo replies being received from random sites on the
Internet when no outbound echo was sent.  As we were doing security
research at the time with IDSes, we spend some time looking into it.

We reported it to the network operations guys, but they really weren't
interested.  We had suspected hanky-panky with ping spoofing, but they
didn't want to deal with it and told us no routing/firewall rules were
in place to prevent spoofing like this, so the real source of the echo
requests could be anywhere within the (rather large) campus network.

Then a couple of months later, the main college routers to the Internet
went down.  The network guys were obviously interested in that.  The
investigated and found out that it died because of an enormous amount of
ICMP traffic coming to/from the campus.  They finally traced it back to
a few Solaris workstations that had been compromised and were used for
DoSing poor bastards on the Internet.

So, what is your network's source IP restriction policy?  In my case,
the echo replies were coming from hosts on the Internet because the
attackers were spoofing my IPs when sending out.  In your case, why
would an attacker try to bounce traffic off of an internal host?  It may
not be malicious. Could it be the result of some broken NAT rule or
something?  Just guessing.  To really find out the answer, you'd
probably have to sit down on 10.11.44.212's local switch and follow MAC 
addresses one router at a time to figure out where the echo requests are
coming from.

HTH,
tim

I have seen this sort of weirdness caused by something completly different.

Check to see if you have a router loop.  If you have a nest of switches
plugged into switches sometimes you can get switch A plugged into switch B
plugged into Switch C which is plugged into switch A.  This causes all
sorts of fun on the network.

Another possibility is that you have a failing switch that is flaking and
throwing in bogus packets or delaying things randomly.

On Thu, 28 Feb 2008, Richard C. Steffens wrote:

> Finally getting to this.

> KDE version :	3.5.4

   More knowledgeable folks will provide higher quality answers, but I'll
offer some thoughts. For example, why are you running KDE on a machine
acting as a server?

> cron.hourly: kmod*
>
> cron.daily: lograte* slocate*

   That looks OK. Nothing polling the printer in there.

> As far as what services are running, does the output of ps ax answer the
> question? (It's below.)

   Yes.

> What tool do I use on Slackware? If it's to not use a tool, but do it
> from the command line, is there some tool I would need to disable?

   ps prints all running processes.

> On SuSE, I start and stop things using YaST.

   Slackware -- until version 12.0 which now uses the SysV init scripts
rather than the BSD init scripts -- has the startup scripts in /etc/rc.d/.
Each application has its own rc.* script and you can append 'start,'
'restart,' or 'stop' to the name of the script.

> The machine has been running for a couple of hours and so far, no issue
> with the network printer. On the other hand, my wife reminds me that it
> was several days before the problem showed up. I don't recall if that's
> true, but I have no reason to doubt her, either.

   Then it may not be anything to do with this one machine. Unless something
new starts after a few days, it does not seem reasonable to me that it would
suddenly start acting like a character in a Stephen King novel or Twilight
Zone episode.

> One other issue for now: SAMBA is working, and I can see the files on
> Slack-2 from this machine. httpd is running, and from Firefox on Slack-2

   If Slack-2 is your server in the basement, why have firefox installed?

> I can connect to http://localhost/ and see index.html correctly
> displayed. However, I can't connect to it from Firefox on this machine.
> If I enter slack-2 in the Firefox address box, I get a Google page. On
> the other hand, if I enter slack-2 in the Firefox address box on my XP
> laptop, I do get the right page. Also, I can ssh from Slack-2 to this
> machine, but not from this machine to Slack-2.

   To see what various network hosts can see, look at /etc/hosts,
/etc/hosts.allow, and /etc/hosts.deny. Also. /etc/hosts.allow controls who
is able to use ssh and what hosts can be accessed.

environment. I don't expect to run X or KDE when it's back in the basement.

>> As far as what services are running, does the output of ps ax answer the

don't? I know I won't be printing, so I don't need CUPS. When I saw kmod
 in the hourly script my first thought was that it was somehow related
to KDE, and that since I won't be running X, I won't need KDE. I tried
to read a man page on kmod, but there isn't one. I did a Google search
and learned that it is a kernel module loader. That sounds like
something I should not mess with.

Is the process (for figuring out what services do) to take every thing
in the output of ps ax that ends with "d" and run a Google search to
learn what it is, or is there a better place to search for that information?

On Fri, 29 Feb 2008, Richard C. Steffens wrote:

> OK. How do I figure out which of those services I need and which I don't?

> Is the process (for figuring out what services do) to take every thing in
> the output of ps ax that ends with "d" and run a Google search to learn
> what it is, or is there a better place to search for that information?

   What I'd do is decide what non-kernel services I want to run; e.g., httpd,
sshd, postfix, whatever. That is, what do you want this machine to do. Then
I would explicitly enable those services and leave the rest as they are.

   As I understand the point of the exercise is to see if this host somehow
causes the network printer to rumble and complain now and then. If that's
the case, then let's focus on what might be doing this -- CUPS -- and ignore
the rest for now.

> OK, but what do I do to tell Slackware not to run those scripts at boot
> time? I'd like to make the changes relatively permanent, so that
> recovery from power failures can happen without my involvement.

   chmod a-x rc.<whatever>

   This makes them non-executable. Also, look in /etc/rc.d/rc.local and see
what that loads at the end of the boot process.

> Aha! I added Slack-2 to Moonguide's ...

   Isn't this one of Frank Zappa's kids?

References: <47C85746.1010803@comcast.net>
	<3d5138980802291108k337cd062gf848af6f31e3adb4@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <alpine.OSX.1.00.0802291131310.4848@arrowhead.galois.com>

On Fri, 29 Feb 2008, Mark Turner wrote:

> cat /etc/slackware-version

I've often wished/hoped for a universal version of this file, 
something like /etc/linux-release with a simple whitespace-separated 
format, with the third field being optional:

<distribution name> <version> [<nickname>]

Shell scripts that need to work across various distributions and 
releases, installers for ISVs, and utilities like cfengine would all 
benefit from not having to do the same inefficient walk through /etc

   does /etc/redhat-release exist?

   how about /etc/debian_version?

   or ubuntu or gentoo or mandriva or ...?

Dumb, dumb.

-- 
Paul Heinlein <> heinlein at madboa.com <> http://www.madboa.com/

or:
$ lsb_release -h

usage: lsb_release [options]

options:
  -h, --help         show this help message and exit
  -v, --version      show LSB modules this system supports
  -i, --id           show distributor ID
  -d, --description  show description of this distribution
  -r, --release      show release number of this distribution
  -c, --codename     show code name of this distribution
  -a, --all          show all of the above information
  -s, --short        show all of the above information in short format

or for what Paul wanted:
$ lsb_release -rc
Description:	Ubuntu 6.06.2 LTS
Codename:	dapper

Alias /viewvc 
/usr/lib/python2.4/site-packages/viewvc/bin/mod_python/viewvc.py
Alias /viewvc-static /usr/share/viewvc/templates/docroot

<Directory /usr/lib/python2.4/site-packages/viewvc/bin/mod_python>
     AddHandler python-program .py
     PythonHandler handler
     PythonPath 
"sys.path+['/usr/lib/python2.4/site-packages/viewvc/bin/mod_pyth\on']"
     Order allow,deny
#    Allow from 127.0.0.1
#    Allow from 168.192.1
     Allow from all

This is a CentOS 5.1 system with subversion-1.4.2-2.el5,

From johnxj at comcast.net  Fri Feb 29 23:19:52 2008
From: johnxj at comcast.net (John Jason Jordan)
Date: Fri, 29 Feb 2008 23:19:52 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Bluetooth and modules and stuff
Message-ID: <20080229231952.f5ddcd5f.johnxj@comcast.net>

On my Gutsy x86_64 laptop my bluetooth mouse works a charm, that is,
when it works. But every now and then it just stops working. Google
found me a fix that until now has solved the problem - "sudo hidd
--search." I don't know enough about how bluetooth works, but until
this evening this has always restored the mouse to normal operation.

Tondight, however, the command has failed. In fact, what I get is:

jjj at Devil7:~$ sudo hidd --search
[sudo] password for jjj:
Searching ...
        Connecting to device 00:0F:F6:6C:6C:DB
Can't get device information: Operation already in progress

I have googled and googled and can't find out exactly what the
"operation already in progress" error message means. Like, what
operation? Can I kill it?

I can restore the mouse function by rebooting, but that is not always
an option. This evening the mouse quit while in the middle of a project
where I was mentally keeping track of the creation of dozens of PDF
files out of various text files. I really didn't want to lose my train
of thought, which is what would have happened if I had shut down all
applications and rebooted. Things like this always happen at the most
annoying moment. In this case I connected a USB mouse temporarily while
I finished the project. 

I ran "lsmod" and the only module relating to bluetooth seems to be
"bluetooth." I tried "rmmod bluetooth' (intending to do an "insmod
bluetooth" afterwards), but I got an error message that several
currently running things were using it.

Other than the stupid stuff that I find on the net ("bluetooth uses
radio ..."), does anyone know how it really works? Does anyone have any
suggestions for command line things that will kill/restore the mouse
when it suddenly dies? Any suggestions welcome!
